                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">آل</orth>
                  </form>, aor. <foreign lang="ar">يَؤُولُ</foreign>, (T, S, M, &amp;c.,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">أَوْلٌ</foreign> (T, M, Mgh, Msb, K) and <foreign lang="ar">مَآلٌ</foreign> (M, K) and <foreign lang="ar">إِيَالٌ</foreign>, which last is used as a subst. in relation to objects of the mind, (Msb,) and <foreign lang="ar">أَيْلُولَةٌ</foreign> [like <foreign lang="ar">دَيْمُومَةٌ</foreign>], (TA,) <hi rend="ital">He,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it, returned;</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">رَجَعَ</foreign>; (T, S, M, Mgh, Msb, K;) and <foreign lang="ar">عَادَ</foreign>; (T;) [and <hi rend="ital">he resorted;</hi> (see an instance voce <foreign lang="ar">إِيَّلٌ</foreign>;)] <foreign lang="ar">إِلَيْهِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">to it;</hi> (M, K;) namely a thing [of any kind; the thing, or place, whence he, or it, originated, or came; his, or its, origin, or source; his, or its, original state, condition, quantity, weight, &amp;c.; any place; and a former action, or saying, or the like: see <foreign lang="ar">رَجَعَ</foreign>, by which, as the explanation of <foreign lang="ar">آلَ</foreign>, may be meant to be implied some other significations, here following, which these two verbs have in common]: (M:) and <foreign lang="ar">آلَ عَنْهُ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">he</hi> (a man, M) <hi rend="ital">returned,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">reverted, from it.</hi> (M, K.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  From <foreign lang="ar">آلَ</foreign> as syn. with <foreign lang="ar">رَجَعَ</foreign> is the phrase, <foreign lang="ar">فُلَانٌ يَؤُولُ إِلَى كَرَمٍ</foreign> [meaning either <hi rend="ital">Such a one returns to generosity,</hi> or, as <foreign lang="ar">كَرَمٌ</foreign> is used in the sense of <foreign lang="ar">كِرَامٌ</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">is referable to generous,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">noble, ancestors</hi>]. (TA.) [And hence the phrase,] <foreign lang="ar">آلَ إِلَيْهِ بِنَسَبٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He bore a relation to him, as a member to a head, by kindred</hi>], and <foreign lang="ar">بِدِينٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">by religion</hi>]. (Ibn-'Arafeh.) And the saying, in a trad., <foreign lang="ar">مَنْ صَامَ الدَّهْرَ فَلَا</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">صَامَ وَ لَا آلَ</foreign>, i. e. <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  [<hi rend="ital">He who fasts ever,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">always, may he neither fast] nor return to what is good.</hi> (TA.) [In the Mgh, art. <foreign lang="ar">دهر</foreign>, for <foreign lang="ar">آل</foreign> I find <foreign lang="ar">أَفْطَرَ</foreign>; and it is there said that this is an imprecation uttered by the Prophet, lest a man should believe <pb n="126"/> this kind of fasting to be ordained by God; or, through impotence, should become insincere; or because, by fasting all the days of the year, he would do so on the days on which fasting is forbidden. See other readings voce <foreign lang="ar">أَلَا</foreign> in art. <foreign lang="ar">الو</foreign>.])          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  Hence also the saying, <foreign lang="ar">آلتِ الضَّرْبَهُ إِلَى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">النَّفْسِ</foreign>, meaning <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">The blow,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">stroke, resulted in destroying life; in slaying,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">killing.</hi> (Mgh.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  Hence also, <foreign lang="ar">آلَ الأَمْرُ إِلَى كَذَا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">The affair,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">case, became ultimately reduced to such a state,</hi>  or <hi rend="ital">condition; came to such a result; came to be thus</hi>]. (Msb.)          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  Hence also, <foreign lang="ar">طَبَخْتُ الشَّرَابَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">فَآلَ إِلَى قَدْرِ كَذَا</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">I cooked the wine,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">beverage, and it became reduced</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">رَجَعَ</foreign>) <hi rend="ital">to such a quantity.</hi> (S.) And <foreign lang="ar">طَبَخَهُ حَتَّى آلَ إِلَى الثُّلُثِ أَوِالرُّبعِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He cooked it</hi> (namely <foreign lang="ar">نَبِيذ</foreign> [i. e. must, or mead, or wort,]) <hi rend="ital">until it became reduced</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">رَجَعَ</foreign>) <hi rend="ital">to the third, or to the fourth:</hi> (T:) or, said of the same, (Mgh,) or of medicine, (TA,) <foreign lang="ar">حَتَّى آلَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">المَنَّانِ مَنَّا وَاحِدًا</foreign>, (Mgh,) or <foreign lang="ar">إِلَى مَنٍّ وَاحِدٍ</foreign>, (TA,) <hi rend="ital">until twice the quantity,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">weight, of a</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">مَنّ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">became</hi> [<hi rend="ital">reduced to</hi>] (<foreign lang="ar">صَارَ</foreign>) <hi rend="ital">one</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">مَنّ</foreign>. (Mgh.)          <sense type="b" n="6">-b6-</sense>  [Hence also, <foreign lang="ar">مَجَازُ الأَوْلِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">The proleptic,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">anticipative, trope;</hi> as <foreign lang="ar">فَصِيلٌ</foreign> applied to “a young camel” before it is weaned, because it is to be weaned.]          <sense type="b" n="7">-b7-</sense>  [And hence also, app.,] <foreign lang="ar">آلَ الشَّىْءُ</foreign>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">مَآلٌ</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">The thing</hi> [<hi rend="ital">became reduced in quantity</hi> or <hi rend="ital">size;</hi>] <hi rend="ital">decreased; diminished;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became defective,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">deficient.</hi> (M, K.) And <foreign lang="ar">آلَ لَحْمُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">النَّاقَةِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">The flesh of the she-camel went away, so that she became lean,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">slender and lean,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">lean and lank in the belly.</hi> (T, K.)          <sense type="b" n="8">-b8-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">آلَ</foreign>, (T, S, M, K,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">أَوْلٌ</foreign> (T, M, K) and <foreign lang="ar">إِيَالٌ</foreign>, (M, K,) is also said of tar, (T, S, M,) and of honey, (S,) and of milk, (M,) and of wine, or beverage, (TA,) and of urine, (M,) or of the urine of camels that have been contented with green pasture instead of water, at the end of their being in that state, (T,) and of oil, (M, K,) and other things, (K,) as meaning <hi rend="ital">It became thick:</hi> (T, S, M, K:) said of milk, <hi rend="ital">it thickened and coagulated:</hi> (M:) said of wine, or beverage, <hi rend="ital">it thickened, and became intoxicating in its utmost degree:</hi> (Az, TA:) and said of oil, <hi rend="ital">it attained its full perfume,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">sweetness of odour, by being well prepared</hi> or <hi rend="ital">compounded.</hi> (T.)          <sense type="b" n="9">-b9-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">مَا لَكَ تَؤُولُ إِلَى كَتِفَيْكَ</foreign> [written in the TA without any vowel-signs, app. meaning <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">What aileth thee that thou shruggest thy shoulders?</hi> lit., <hi rend="ital">drawest thyself together to thy two shoulder-blades?</hi>] is said [to a man] <foreign lang="ar">إِذَا</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">ٱنْضَمَّ إِلَيْهِمَا وَٱجْتَمَعَ</foreign> [when he draws himself together to them, and contracts himself]; and is a tropical phrase: so says Z. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="10">-b10-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">آلَ مِنْ</foreign>

      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n1499-6" target="تأوّلهُ" n="6" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, (M, K,) inf. n. of the former as above, (K,) when said of language, signify <foreign lang="ar">دَبَّرَهُ وَقَدَّرَهُ وَفَسَّرَهُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">he considered its end,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">what it might be to which it led or pointed, and compared one part of it with another, and</hi> then <hi rend="ital">explained,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">expounded,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">interpreted, it</hi>]: (M, K:) hence, [if the explanation in the M and K be meant to denote three distinct meanings, which I do not think to be the case,] it would seem as though <foreign lang="ar">تَأْوِيلٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">تَفْسِيرٌ</foreign> were syn.; but accord. to other authorities, they differ: (TA:) [Az says,] accord. to Ahmad Ibn-Yahyà, these two words and <foreign lang="ar">مَعْنًى</foreign> are all one: but <foreign lang="ar">تأويل</foreign> seems to me to signify the <hi rend="ital">collecting the meanings of dubious expressions by such expression as is clear,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">plain, without dubiousness:</hi> or, accord. to Lth, it is the <hi rend="ital">interpreting of language that has different meanings; and this cannot be rightly done but by an explanation which changes the expression;</hi> as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n1499-7" target="تأَوُّلٌ" n="7" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>: (T:) or the <hi rend="ital">turning a verse of the Kur-án from its apparent meaning to a meaning which it bears,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">admits, when the latter is agreeable with the Scripture and the Sunneh:</hi> for instance, in the words of the Kur [vi. 95, &amp;c.], <foreign lang="ar">يُخْرِجُ ٱلْحَىَّ مِنَ المَيِّتِ</foreign>, if the meaning be [thus explained] “He produceth the bird from the egg,” this is <foreign lang="ar">تفسير</foreign>: and if [it be explained as meaning] “He produceth the believer from the unbeliever,” or “the knowing from the ignorant,” this is <foreign lang="ar">تأويل</foreign>: so says Ibn-El-Kemál: (TA:) [hence, although it may often be rendered by <hi rend="ital">interpretation,</hi> like <foreign lang="ar">تفسير</foreign>, it more properly signifies the <hi rend="ital">rendering in a manner not according to the letter,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">overt sense; explaining the covert,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">virtual,</hi> 
                  <pb n="127"/> 
                  <hi rend="ital">meaning; interpreting in a manner not according to the obvious meaning:</hi>] or the <hi rend="ital">reducing a thing to its ultimate intent, whether it be a saying or an action:</hi> (Er-Rághib, TA:) or <foreign lang="ar">تفسير</foreign> signifies the “discovering, detecting, revealing, or disclosing, what is meant by a dubious expression;” and <foreign lang="ar">تأويل</foreign>, the <hi rend="ital">reducing one of two senses,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">interpretations, which an expression bears,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">admits, to that which suits the apparent meaning:</hi> (L and K in art. <foreign lang="ar">فسر</foreign>, and TA in that and in the present art.:) or the former signifies the “expounding, explaining, or interpreting, the narratives which occur collected without discrimination in the Kur-án, and making known the significations of the strange words or expressions, and explaining the occasions on which the verses were revealed;” and the latter, the <hi rend="ital">explaining the meaning of that which is</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">مُتَشَابِهِ</foreign>, [or <hi rend="ital">what is equivocal,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">ambiguous,</hi>] i. e., <hi rend="ital">what is not understood without repeated consideration.</hi> (TA: [in which are some further explanations; but these add nothing of importance.])          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  [Hence, <foreign lang="ar">أوّل لَفْظًا</foreign>, in grammar, <hi rend="ital">He rendered a word,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">an expression,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">a phrase, in grammatical analysis, by another word,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">expression,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">phrase.</hi>]          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  And [hence likewise,] <foreign lang="ar">تَأْوِيلٌ</foreign> signifies also The <hi rend="ital">interpretation,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">explanation,</hi> of a dream; the <hi rend="ital">telling the final sequel,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">result,</hi> thereof: (M, K:) as in the Kur xii. 101.                   <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">آلٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">آل</orth>
                  </form> A man's <foreign lang="ar">أَهْل</foreign> [or <hi rend="ital">family</hi>]; (T, S, M, Msb, K;) i. e. his <hi rend="ital">relations:</hi> (Msb:) his <foreign lang="ar">عَشِيرَة</foreign> [or <hi rend="ital">kinsfolk;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">nearer,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">nearest, relations by descent from the same father or ancestor;</hi> &amp;c.]; from <foreign lang="ar">أَوْلٌ</foreign> as signifying <foreign lang="ar">رُجُوعٌ</foreign>, because recourse is had to them in all affairs: (Har p. 578:) and his <hi rend="ital">household;</hi> (S, TA;) the <hi rend="ital">people of</hi> his <hi rend="ital">house:</hi> (Msb:) and his <hi rend="ital">followers;</hi> (S, Msb, K;) including <hi rend="ital">soldiers:</hi> (S, TA:) and his <foreign lang="ar">أَوْلِيَآء</foreign> [i. e. <hi rend="ital">friends,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">the like</hi>]: (K:) <hi rend="ital">those who bear a relation</hi> to him, <hi rend="ital">as members to a head,</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">مَنْ آلَ إِلَيْهِ</foreign>,) <hi rend="ital">by religion</hi> or <hi rend="ital">persuasion</hi> or <hi rend="ital">kindred;</hi> as in the Kur iii. 9 and viii. 54 and 56 &amp;c.: (Ibn-'Arafeh:) [or in these and many other instances, it may be rendered <hi rend="ital">people:</hi>] but in general it is not used save in relation to that in which is eminence, or nobility; so that one does not say, <foreign lang="ar">آلُ الإِسْكَافِ</foreign>, like as one says <foreign lang="ar">أَهْلُهُ</foreign>: (K:) and it is peculiarly used as a prefix to the proper names of rational beings; not to indeterminate nouns, nor to nouns of places or of times; so that one says, <foreign lang="ar">آلُ فُلَانٍ</foreign>; but not <foreign lang="ar">آلُ رَجُلٍ</foreign>, nor <foreign lang="ar">آلُ زَمَانِ كَذَا</foreign>, nor <foreign lang="ar">آلُ مَوْضَعِ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">كَذَا</foreign>, like as one says, [<foreign lang="ar">أَهْلُ رَجُلٍ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">أَهْلُ زَمَانِ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">كَذَا</foreign>, and] <foreign lang="ar">أَهْلُ بَلَدِ كَذَا</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">مَوْضِعِ كَذَا</foreign>: (TA:) Ks disallows its being prefixed to a pronoun; so that one should not say, <foreign lang="ar">آلُهُ</foreign>, but <foreign lang="ar">أَهْلُهُ</foreign>; but his opinion in this matter is not correct: it is originally <foreign lang="ar">أَوَلٌ</foreign>; the <foreign lang="ar">و</foreign> being changed into <foreign lang="ar">ا</foreign>, (M, * Msb,) as in <foreign lang="ar">قَالَ</foreign> [which is originally <foreign lang="ar">قَوَلَ</foreign>]: so say some: (Msb:) or it is originally <foreign lang="ar">أَهْلٌ</foreign>, (T, M, Msb, K,) then <foreign lang="ar">أَأْلٌ</foreign>, and then <foreign lang="ar">آلٌ</foreign>: (K:) so say some, arguing thus from its having <foreign lang="ar">أُهَيْلٌ</foreign> for its dim.: (T, Msb:) but accord. to Ks, it assumes the form   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n1501-1" target="أُوَيْلٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> as a dim.: (T:) or each of these is its dim. (M, K.) By the <foreign lang="ar">آل</foreign> of the Prophet are meant, accord. to some persons, <hi rend="ital">His followers, whether relations or others:</hi> and <hi rend="ital">his relations, whether followers or not:</hi> (Ahmad Ibn-Yahyà, T:) or, as some say, <hi rend="ital">his family</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">أَهْلُهُ</foreign> [q. v.]) <hi rend="ital">and his wives:</hi> [but it seems to be indicated that what I have rendered “and his wives” is meant as an explicative adjunct to <foreign lang="ar">اهله</foreign>:] or, as some say, <hi rend="ital">the people of his religion:</hi> (Esh-Sháfi'ee, T:) being himself asked who were his <foreign lang="ar">آل</foreign>, he answered <hi rend="ital">all pious persons:</hi> (Anas, TA:) but in a trad. in which it is said that the poor-rates are prohibited to him and to his <foreign lang="ar">آل</foreign>, by this is meant those to whom was appropriated the fifth [of the spoils] instead of the poor-rates; and these were the genuine descendants of Háshim and El-Muttalib. (Esh-Sháfi'ee, T.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">يَا لَزَيْدٍ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">يَالَ زَيْدٍ</foreign>, accord. to the Koofees, are contractions of <foreign lang="ar">يَا آلَ زَيْدٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">O family of Zeyd</hi>].
